dmidecode -- especially for anything associated with your system's 
mainboard: BIOS revision, memory configuration, on-board controllers, 
etc.

John Jason Jordan wrote:
> On Wed, 28 Feb 2007 21:25:37 -0800
> "Kok, Auke" <sofar at foo-projects.org> dijo:
> 
>> there's a debian package called `discover` that collects pci, usb, pcmcia device 
>> ID's and appropriate drivers (mostly kernel modules, but also x.org driver name).
>>
>> should be available through apt I think. `discover` and `discover-data`
> 
> I found it in Synaptic, where the current version seems to be discover
> 1 and discover1-data. Both were already installed. I tried running it
> from the command line but it didn't work:
> 
> jjj at Devil5:~$ discover
> open_sock(): Operation not permitted
> jjj at Devil5:~$ sudo discover
> Password:
> jjj at Devil5:~$ sudo discover1
> sudo: discover1: command not found
> jjj at Devil5:~$ sudo discover
> jjj at Devil5:~$ 
> 
> I googled and discovered that it doesn't really "work." It is used to
> detect hardware during bootup. So it doesn't create a report or
> anything I could put into a text document.

discover-modprobe -v

on my machine:

Discovering hardware: intel-agp uhci-hcd ehci-hcd snd-intel8x0 snd-intel8x0m 
i8xx_tco ahci i2c-i801 radeonfb tg3 yenta_socket ipw2200
Loading intel-agp:
Loading uhci-hcd:
Loading ehci-hcd:
Loading snd-intel8x0:
Loading snd-intel8x0m:
Loading i8xx_tco:
FATAL: Error inserting i8xx_tco 
(/lib/modules/2.6.19.2/kernel/drivers/char/watchdog/i8xx_tco.ko): No such device
Skipping ahci; assuming it is compiled into the kernel.
Loading i2c-i801:
Skipping radeonfb; assuming it is compiled into the kernel.
Skipping Module tg3. It's already loaded.
Skipping yenta_socket; assuming it is compiled into the kernel.
Skipping Module ipw2200. It's already loaded.

also, since it's xml-based, it's trivial to have it `just return` the modules:

$ discover --data-path=linux/module/name --data-path=linux/module/options 
--format="%s %s" --data-version=2.6
intel-agp
uhci-hcd
uhci-hcd
uhci-hcd
uhci-hcd
ehci-hcd
snd-intel8x0
snd-intel8x0m
i8xx_tco
ahci
i2c-i801
radeonfb
tg3
yenta_socket
ipw2200


Cheers,

Auke


From qhartman at gmail.com  Thu Mar  1 07:58:22 2007
From: qhartman at gmail.com (Quentin Hartman)
Date: Thu, 1 Mar 2007 07:58:22 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] VMWare question: How to start vmware guests automatically
In-Reply-To: <eac729460703010104o221675a4odc3949eee4359980@mail.gmail.com>
References: <eac729460703010104o221675a4odc3949eee4359980@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <8975a95f0703010758w50de89a3ya0231e7c3c1e520b@mail.gmail.com>

On 3/1/07, David Mandel <dmandel at pdxlinux.org> wrote:
>
> I have VMWare Workstation 5.x up and running.
> It works great, but I have always used it interactively.
> Is there a way to start vmware guest machines automatically
> at system boot or from a crontab or whatever?
> Do I need to install VMWare server for this?
>

As Andy mentioned, this is a VMware server feature, however VMware
Workstation 6 (which is currently in Free Beta) can run VM's "disconnected",
which is effectively the same. It should be trivial to script up something
to start them automatically using the "vmrun" command. FWIW, I've been using
the 6 beta since it's first release, and have had no problems.

-- 
-Regards-

-Quentin Hartman-

Still doesn't work. I just get Command Not Found. But now it's morning
and I'm thinking more clearly. I'm wondering if there might be
something else that would be easier. 

To reiterate the problem: Everything on my Edgy amd64 installation
works just fine except OOo. Unfotunately, I *live* in OOo. There are
three basic problems: Drag and drop editing of text does not work, the
web page wizard crashes OOo, and features set in Tools > Options are
not being saved to the default template. The latter is especially
annoying because every time I open a document I have to go into Tools >
Options and change the settings, and as soon as I save, close and
reopen the document I have to do it all over again. I have been
struggling with this since December. I have at least 50 hours invested
in trying to fix this and probably twice that much.

The only version available in the Edgy amd64 repositories is 2.0.4. I
did manage to install 2.1, but the problems did not go away. I also
used the Edgy live/install 32-bit CD and OOo worked fine, but when I
used the 64-bit live/install CD the problems were still there. Since
the problems also occur with the 64-bit live/install CD, I conclude
that I can stop fiddling with my installation of OOo 2.0.4 and I can
stop trying to fix something in my Edgy installation. If it is still
broken when using the 64-bit live/install CD, then there must be
something conflicting with my hardware with 64-bit Edgy. There are a
few others who have the same problem and I wanted to have them all tell
me about their hardware so I could look for commonalities. Hence, my
search for a command that would get me a list of all their hardware.

But after sleeping on it I am now thinking in a different direction.
Back in the days of Breezy I used a 32-bit chroot environment to run
Firefox and Adobe Reader. When Dapper came out I was able to get both
working acceptably in the 64-bit world, so I got rid of the 32-bit
chroot environment. Maybe I should set a 32-bit chroot environment back
up again and install OOo in it. I'm assuming that this will fix the
problem because OOo runs fine from the 32-bit live/install CD.

I also thought about just installing 32bit OOo with
--force-architecture. I'm not sure that can be done -- it's a pretty
big program that comes with a lot of different .debs. Plus, I think the
current OOo 2.0.4 actually is the 32-bit OOo, Ubuntu-ized to run in
64-bit Edgy. 

I can also set up a chroot to run Dapper, either 32- or 64-bit (there
is a how-to on Ubuntu forums). 

The reason I am now thinking along these lines is that, even assuming
the others who have been bitten by this bug and I can manage to isolate
whatever is causing the problem, it will probably require a fix from
Ubuntu, and by the time that is available Feisty will have been
released. In fact, Ubuntu probably won't even bother to fix Edgy. I
filed a bug report
(https://launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/openoffice.org-amd64/+bug/85248)
on February 15 and no one at Ubuntu has even bothered to reply or
assign it to anyone. 

I am open to any suggestions. Maybe someone can think of something even
simpler that will do as well.

From qhartman at gmail.com  Thu Mar  1 10:34:31 2007
From: qhartman at gmail.com (Quentin Hartman)
Date: Thu, 1 Mar 2007 10:34:31 -0800
Subject: [lug] Re: [PLUG] VMWare question: How to start vmware guests
	automatically
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0703010932140.23513@venus.cds1.net>
References: <eac729460703010104o221675a4odc3949eee4359980@mail.gmail.com>
	<8975a95f0703010758w50de89a3ya0231e7c3c1e520b@mail.gmail.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.61.0703010932140.23513@venus.cds1.net>
Message-ID: <8975a95f0703011034h6d1a46a6l919f6b47f651b944@mail.gmail.com>

On 3/1/07, Brian Wilson <brian at wildsong.biz> wrote:
>
> > As Andy mentioned, this is a VMware server feature, however VMware
> > Workstation 6 (which is currently in Free Beta) can run VM's
> "disconnected",
>
> Having owned and upgraded VMWare Workstation since it came out,
> it's hard for me to understand why I'd want to use it in preference
> to VMWare Server to use as a SERVER, when VMWare Server is free.


David didn't inidcate whether or not he was wanting a machine to be running
as a "server", only that he wanted it to start automatically and he already
had workstation installed and running. Your point is well taken though, and
for many people, using server when you need a vm to start at boot is the
right answer. However workstation has some advantages over server in some
situations:

-Better interactive performance - This is according to VMware support
directly.
-Support for multiple snapshots - server can only do one at a time.
-Clone a VM - This can be relatively easily done by hand, but the
workstation UI makes it completely brainless
-VM Teaming - Tremendously useful for setting up complex test environments,
even if they are "server" class.
-Support for multiple monitors (6 beta only)
-Support for USB 2.0 at full speed (6 beta only)

So, Workstation is targetted squarely at testing / development and server at
production. However, it's entirely possible that some production needs would
require the use of Workstation (or moving up to ESX) or that testing needs
could be met by server.

-- 
-Regards-

-Quentin Hartman-

On 3/1/07, Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> wrote:
>    My reboot yesterday lost sound capabilities. While I wait for a reply to
> my post to the alsa mail list, I hope someone here can explain why I cannot
> load the snd_intel8x0.ko module.
>
> [root at salmo /lib/modules/2.6.19.2/kernel/sound/pci]# modprobe
> ./snd-intel8x0.ko
> FATAL: Module ./snd_intel8x0.ko not found.
>
>    This module was built with the kernel, and I'm telling modprobe just where
> it is, so why cannot modprobe find it?
>

I think that you just give the name of the module to modprobe, and it
looks for it in
/lib/modules/loaded-kernel/.

Did you perhaps boot into a new kernel, for which the snd module has
not been built?

Or if it is in the tree, try modprobing it again, leaving off the './'.

On Thu, 1 Mar 2007, Ali Corbin wrote:

> Did you perhaps boot into a new kernel, for which the snd module has not
> been built?

Ali, et al.:

   No, it's the same 2.6.19.2 since January. For whatever the reason, the
kernel .config file did not have SND-INTEL8X0 set to module. So, I changed
that, rebuilt and reinstalled modules, and modprobe then loaded
snd-intel8x0.

   Ran alsaconf and it found the chip, made sure everything was installed and
running, then told me to go have fun after adjusting sound with my favorite
mixer. Well, it's back to the ALSA wiki troubleshooting page because aumix
won't load and alsamixer shows nothing but the header. Progress, but not yet
all there.

Thanks,

Rich

A couple comments:

(1)  Actually, VMWare Server is free - free as in no cost - not free
as in freedom.
      See: http://www.vmware.com/products/free_virtualization.html for details.

(2)  VMWare workstation costs money.
      I own a copy or two of VMWare workstation 5.x
      I should try VMWare workstation 6.0 beta.  I have not.

(3)  VMWare workstation will do a lot that VMWare Server won't do.
      Thus, I'm using VMWare workstation.
      Unfortunately, the documentation says you can NOT run workstation
      and server on the same computer, and the command line interface
      for VMWare Workstation stinks.  (Or maybe I don't understand
      it's features.)

(4)  Mostly, I use VMWare to run Linux under Linux
      I haven't quite figured networking out for Xen yet.
      Xen seems to work great, but there doesn't seem to be an easy
      strait forward way of creating Xen virtual machines.
      Eventually, I intend to use VMWare to create Xen virtual
      machines as needed and use Xen to run these.
      In the mean time, I'm using VMWare on one machine for everything
      and that is why I would like my VMWare guests to start automatically
      on boot.

Date: Thu, 1 Mar 2007 12:28:15 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Another Post-Reboot Issue: PostgreSQL
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0702280706520.11941@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0702280706520.11941@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <53107f6e0703011228k5841cbcevae9cfd182f3ebb21@mail.gmail.com>

Try adding, to the bottom of /var/lib/postgres/data/pg_hba.conf:
local all all trust

If that works, you should then change to more restricted 'trust' (for
security purposes), etc.

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Thu Mar  1 12:34:46 2007
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Thu, 1 Mar 2007 12:34:46 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Another Post-Reboot Issue: PostgreSQL
In-Reply-To: <53107f6e0703011228k5841cbcevae9cfd182f3ebb21@mail.gmail.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0702280706520.11941@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<53107f6e0703011228k5841cbcevae9cfd182f3ebb21@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0703011232170.23822@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Thu, 1 Mar 2007, Jon Scully wrote:

> Try adding, to the bottom of /var/lib/postgres/data/pg_hba.conf:
> local all all trust

Jon,

   Tom Lane identified the problem. The network socket in /tmp was owned by
root.root instead of by postgres.users.

   I learned that I could remove that file after stopping the postmaster, and
that it was recreated properly when the postmaster was restarted. That fixed
the problem. I had no idea that I could safely wipe out that socket file;
that's why I didn't touch it until told it was a good thing to do.

Thanks,

Rich

I can recommend CTL laptops for Linux compatibility, though at least from
what I can see they don't sell them without Windows.  Perhaps if you ask
their salescritters directly.  Its not an option on the website.
http://www.ctlnotebooks.com/v2/default.aspx

I have a laptop not from CTL but from the OEM that they use, Compal (one of
the big 3 OEMs- Compal, Clevo, Quanta, that actually manufacture about 95%
of all laptops).
See here for handy reference: http://tuxmobil.org/laptop_oem.html
(poke around the rest of Tuxmobil of you haven't before, handy site)

I have a CL50 bought a couple years ago, currently runs Ubuntu and WinXP,
works like a champ, all hardware works with Linux.  The CL50 is sold by CTL
as Travel Master NB5500.  It is the exact same unit, as the company I work
for uses CTL laptops.  I have been issued a CTL version of the CL56 for work
use, I think they call it TravelMaster NB5600.  Some colleagues have been
issued the CL50. CL56 is almost identical to the CL50 except for color
scheme and better video card (Radeon Mobility 9700 with 128M VRAM).  I have
booted Knoppix with it so far and it all works.  I am seriously considering
repartitioning it and putting Ubuntu on this along side the required Win2K
(it will most likely be reimaged once I turn it back in anyway).  Though I
can't speak for the newer models, as far as the CL50 and CL56 based models
they work with Linux no problem, smooth as melted butter.

I haven't run VMWare for a while because it doesn't work on the low power
boxes I currently use, however, I was able to make version three and
possibly four (I don't remember) of their workstation platform provide

up a full virtual network with half a dozen virtual machines automatically

From kens at cad2cam.com  Thu Mar  1 21:01:20 2007
From: kens at cad2cam.com (Kenneth G. Stephens)
Date: Thu, 01 Mar 2007 21:01:20 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Regaining Lost Sound
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0703011102500.23822@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0703010716080.23822@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<965f90c20703011057x34242cck7a07449f1860447d@mail.gmail.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0703011102500.23822@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <1172811680.3437.6.camel@atlas.cadtocam.com>

On Thu, 2007-03-01 at 11:06 -0800, Rich Shepard wrote:
> On Thu, 1 Mar 2007, Ali Corbin wrote:
> 
> > Did you perhaps boot into a new kernel, for which the snd module has not
> > been built?
> 
> Ali, et al.:
> 
>    No, it's the same 2.6.19.2 since January. For whatever the reason, the
> kernel .config file did not have SND-INTEL8X0 set to module. So, I changed
> that, rebuilt and reinstalled modules, and modprobe then loaded
> snd-intel8x0.
> 
>    Ran alsaconf and it found the chip, made sure everything was installed and
> running, then told me to go have fun after adjusting sound with my favorite
> mixer. Well, it's back to the ALSA wiki troubleshooting page because aumix
> won't load and alsamixer shows nothing but the header. Progress, but not yet
> all there.
> 
> Thanks,
> 
> Rich
> 

Rich,

I just got through the fun of getting my sound back working after
updating my kernel in FC5. Everyonce in a while the updates go just
fine, but this time gmplayer played RocketBoom.com just fine but my
realplayer playing Radio Paradise was silent.  It connected just fine
and looked like it was playing just fine.  But no sound.  I opened kmix
and discovered that realplay was connected to my on motherboard sound
card while I could choose my alsa sound for the gmplayer.  

After much hunting, I discovered a file called /etc/asound.conf.  This
was setup originally like this:
#Generated by system-config-soundcard, do not edit by hand
#SWCONF
#DEV 0
defaults.pcm.card 1
defaults.pcm.device 0
defaults.ctl.card 1

Note the '0' on the pcm.device line.  Went against the admonition and
editted the file by hand and changed the 0 to 1.  Rebooted and realplay
is playing Radio Paradise again.

May not help you a bit, Rich, but I am happier,
now.                                               
-- 
Ken Stephens
CAD 2 CAM



From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Fri Mar  2 06:26:26 2007
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Fri, 2 Mar 2007 06:26:26 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Regaining Lost Sound -- RESTORED
In-Reply-To: <1172811680.3437.6.camel@atlas.cadtocam.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0703010716080.23822@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<965f90c20703011057x34242cck7a07449f1860447d@mail.gmail.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0703011102500.23822@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<1172811680.3437.6.camel@atlas.cadtocam.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0703020610040.30562@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Thu, 1 Mar 2007, Kenneth G. Stephens wrote:

> I just got through the fun of getting my sound back working after updating
> my kernel in FC5. Everyonce in a while the updates go just fine, but this
> time gmplayer played RocketBoom.com just fine but my realplayer playing
> Radio Paradise was silent.  It connected just fine and looked like it was
> playing just fine.  But no sound.  I opened kmix and discovered that
> realplay was connected to my on motherboard sound card while I could
> choose my alsa sound for the gmplayer.

Ken,

   In my case there were seveal factors that contributed to the problem. The
first was that snd-intel8x0.ko was trashed internally. That's why it
wouldn't load. After 'make modules; make modules_installed', it loaded just
fine, but after the snd-usb-audio. Since USB sound has no mixer support (or
minimal at best), neither aumix nor alsamixer would run.

   The second factor was that I had managed to build the 2.6.19.2 kernel
without the ability to rmmod. Can't explain why, but that's what I did.
Ergo, could not remove the sound modules and reinstall them in the proper
order. 'make; make modules; make modules_install;' move files to /boot, run
/sbin/lilo just in case, and a reboot fixed that problem.

   The third factor was sound modules still in the incorrect sequence.
Manually removed them all -- starting with the nVIDIA ones with the most
dependencies and working my way down the list -- followed by 'modprobe
snd-intel8x0' and 'modprobe snd-usb-audio'. Et voila! Eet woiked again.
Curiously, I had to increase the levels of all channels in alsamixer as well
as the pgm channel in aumix to bring the sound to a sufficiently high level.

> After much hunting, I discovered a file called /etc/asound.conf.  This
> was setup originally like this:

   I have an alsa-generated file (with warnings to not touch) in
/etc/modules.conf. However, the modules to be loaded area apparently the
ones in /etc/modprobe.d/sound. A Swiss fellow on the alsa mail list
recommeded that I modify that file (which had only the nVIDIA drivers, the
same as in /etc/modules.conf) to the following:

alias snd-card-0 snd-intel8x0
options snd-intel8x0 index=0
alias snd-card-1 snd-usb-audio
options snd-usb-audio index=1

alias sound-slot-0 snd-card-0
alias sound-slot-1 snd-card-1

   That, he assures me, will keep them in the proper order the next time I
reboot after a kernel change.

Thanks for your input,

Rich

--

Applied Ecosystem Services, Inc.        |          Accelerator(TM)
<http://www.appl-ecosys.com>     Voice: 503-667-4517      Fax: 503-667-8863


From qhartman at gmail.com  Fri Mar  2 06:54:43 2007
From: qhartman at gmail.com (Quentin Hartman)
Date: Fri, 2 Mar 2007 06:54:43 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Any experience with Brother MFC-7820N?
In-Reply-To: <45E782DA.1070602@comcast.net>
References: <45E782DA.1070602@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <8975a95f0703020654o371e0a6cre00691db549f914b@mail.gmail.com>

I don't have experience with that particular model, but I have worked with
other Brother laser printers. They worked fine with CUPS printing system,
and overall I'd rate them as "passable". They were a little slow-ish, and
their output was ok, but not great. They were good enough for what we paid
for them, and good enough for home / very small biz use, but I think if I
had owned them personally, I would have eventually wished I'd spent a little
more money and gotten something a little nicer.

The speed shouldn't be a problem for me. I currently have a Brother

machine to see the parallel port, so I've only used it with 98SE and XP.
On a new drum, it works well. Eventually - after a year or more - the
drum wears out. Unfortunately, that drum is no longer available from the
usual sources, and so there are extra marks on the page due to the
scratches on the drum.

Since I am now in need of a fax machine, and I don't do production
amounts of printing, I figured a multi-function fax/printer would be a
good solution.

As business picks up, I may decide I need a better printer. At that
time, the 7820N will still be a good fax machine. And for now, this
looks like a reasonable approach.

From plug at merlot.com  Fri Mar  2 09:59:36 2007

Quentin Hartman (qhartman at gmail.com) typed this ...
> I don't have experience with that particular model, but I have worked with
> other Brother laser printers. They worked fine with CUPS printing system,
> and overall I'd rate them as "passable". They were a little slow-ish, and
> their output was ok, but not great. They were good enough for what we paid
> for them, and good enough for home / very small biz use, but I think if I
> had owned them personally, I would have eventually wished I'd spent a little

The 7820N doesn't warm up quickly, but it's not a horrible wait unless
you're extremely impatient (10-12 seconds average). The printing is VERY
fast; I don't the the 20ppm rating is an exaggeration.

Text quality is fine (not spectacular, but you have to look hard to find
jaggies), and the graphics quality is closer to what I would call
'passable'; not bad but not great either.

For the price and considering that Brother supports Linux so well, I'm
very happy with mine.

From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Sat Mar  3 12:29:05 2007
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Sat, 3 Mar 2007 12:29:05 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] bind9 on low-spec machine?
Message-ID: <200703031229.05494.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

Hi all,

I've been happily running bind for local nameservices+caching on a 
300MHz k7 with 256MB ram for a couple of years now.  Recently, I've 
been migrating that machine's (fileserver, etc) services to a much 
faster box, but I decided to try DNS on a much lower-powered box (which 
is a failover webserver, etc and rarely gets shutdown.)  The box in 
question is a pentium 133MHz with 128MB ram.  Both machines are running 
sarge.

Now dns queries are extremely slow.  It looks like the box isn't 
swapping, but I haven't got the first clue about diagnosing a bind 
performance issue.  Is it cpu bound?  Something just plain weird with 
this old machine?  The other odd thing is that if I turn off the local 
nameservices (and use just caching), the speed comes back.  Do I just 
have a braindead dns setup (and the faster machine is able to gloss 
over my idiocy?)  Note that I don't claim to know what I'm doing since 
RTFM'ing doesn't seem to be doing me any good here.

Any suggestions?  Should I be looking for a different server daemon?  
What are the embedded linux routers and such running for dns?

--Eric

Eric-
You can set the debug level to 255 which will log EVERYTHING but might be
useful in telling you whats wrong. You can play with the debug levels to get
what you want. When the machine is running slow do you see an increase in
load on the box? What version are you running? How many zones are you
loading? Bind loads the config data and zones into memory at startup so if
you're loading a bunch of zones @ 128 MB of RAM it would make sense that it
speeds back up when you go to a caching only setup.

Drew-

From brian at wildsong.biz  Thu Mar  1 10:04:03 2007
From: brian at wildsong.biz (Brian Wilson)
Date: Thu, 1 Mar 2007 10:04:03 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [lug] Re: [PLUG] VMWare question: How to start vmware guests
	automatically
In-Reply-To: <8975a95f0703010758w50de89a3ya0231e7c3c1e520b@mail.gmail.com>
References: <eac729460703010104o221675a4odc3949eee4359980@mail.gmail.com>
	<8975a95f0703010758w50de89a3ya0231e7c3c1e520b@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0703010932140.23513@venus.cds1.net>

> As Andy mentioned, this is a VMware server feature, however VMware
> Workstation 6 (which is currently in Free Beta) can run VM's "disconnected",

Having owned and upgraded VMWare Workstation since it came out,
it's hard for me to understand why I'd want to use it in preference
to VMWare Server to use as a SERVER, when VMWare Server is free.

You can still build and test your virtual machine(s) using the desktop 
product and then just copy them over to your server (or to VMWare Player), 
if you want. I don't really see any big advantages of Desktop versus
Server yet.

We are currently in the process of virtualizing all our Windows servers.
I rolled out the first one on Tuesday. We will have a development server
running Debian and VMWare Server and a fileserver running Debian and 
Samba. Hardware is dual core dual Xeon 3 Ghz + 4 GB ram + SATA drives.

We run Windows operating systems on servers to allow us to develop
software using ESRI and Oracle products. (Yes, there are Linux
versions of those products but our clients run Windows and IIS.)

We have enough developers and projects now that it was no longer
practical for us to have just one Windows development server. By
virtualizing instead of adding more servers, we can copy an existing
server, upgrade it, and keep the old own filed away for legcay testing
and updates and move on with the new one. The machine is big enough to
run several machines so one developer can be doing legcacy support
while another is testing out the newest release on a separate server.

With the server version of VMWare you can run a console app under X11
on the server or you can run a client on either a Windows or Linux
desktop. There is also a web thing that can do some basic things like
control the VMware daemon itself and tell you what machines are
running. I prefer not to run X11 on my servers so we are using the
Windows client. Generally no one wants to sit near the servers anyway.
Too noisy and cramped.

VMWare is not officially supported on Debian but it works fine. I had
to build a kernel for our configuration so I had to apply a patch to 
VMware to get its modules to build correctly. (This would be true for
any machine running the latest kernel.)

I am looking forward to playing with the perl VMWare Server API. No idea
yet what it can do.

BTW we have a machine running Asterisk and Debian as our office phone
system now too. Saved us a bundle.


Brian Wilson
Alsea Geospatial, Inc

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Sun Mar  4 07:52:17 2007
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Sun, 4 Mar 2007 07:52:17 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] postfix body_checks regexp help needed
In-Reply-To: <45EA27F2.80403@frankhunt.com>
References: <45EA27F2.80403@frankhunt.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0703040737400.4839@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Sat, 3 Mar 2007, Frank Hunt wrote:

> I am using postfix body_checks to filter out some special stuff that was
> getting through spamassassin.  There is a drug who's name I can't type
> here or this will get filtered, that name is contained in the word
> "specialist" (remove the first 3 letters and the last one).  I want to
> filter out that drug name and not filter out the word "specialist" using
> body_checks and regular expressions.

Frank,

   The messages must pass your postfix filters before they're handed off to
spamassassin, not the other way around.

   It does get tricky to trap those specific strings and not when they're
embedded in legitimate words. I have three suggestions for you:

   1) Use the \b symbol to denote the beginning and ending of a word. For
example, your body_checks might contain a line like this
/\b damn \b/		reject 550 Rule B1023

This tells postfix to look for that string of four characters as a single
word set off by white space on either side, and not embedded within another
word. Several years ago I was advised to number each header_check and
body_check rule (thanks, Ed!!) and it makes it so much easier to trace the
rule that triggerd a rejection.

   2) Get a copy of 20_drugs.cf (there are references on the spamassassin
mail list archives) and put it in /usr/share/spamassassin.

   3) Sign on to both the postfix and spamassassin mail lists for a while.
While they're high volume, you'll learn a lot, find answers to almost all of
your questions, and will receive answers to questions you pose.

   A couple of months ago I upgraded my system and for some reason was
overwhelmed with spam. A weeks' worth of time on the maillists, and some
questions for clarification, and my spam-blocking was much more finely
tuned. On average I see 0-5 spam per day now.

-- 
Richard B. Shepard, Ph.D.               |    The Environmental Permitting
Applied Ecosystem Services, Inc.        |          Accelerator(TM)
<http://www.appl-ecosys.com>     Voice: 503-667-4517      Fax: 503-667-8863

On Mon, 5 Mar 2007, Richard C. Steffens wrote:

> In Excel, if one tabs from column to column while entering data and then
> hits <ENTER>, the active cell becomes the cell below the one from which
> tabbing began. In OOcalc, <ENTER> just moves you to the cell below the one
> you were on when you hit <ENTER>.

Dick,

   Tools -> Options -> OOcalc.

   Input settings -> top checkbox "Press Enter to move selection;" the drop
down box to the right defaults (here) to "Down." Other choices are "Up,",
"Right," "Left."

Rich

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Mon Mar  5 17:54:09 2007
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Mon, 5 Mar 2007 17:54:09 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Need Help "SSH through VPN"
In-Reply-To: <a49cba240703051441v183a709en95c8697202a4b610@mail.gmail.com>
References: <a49cba240703051441v183a709en95c8697202a4b610@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20070306015409.GA10266@gate.kl-ic.com>

On Mon, Mar 05, 2007 at 02:41:12PM -0800, Jenifer Chung wrote:
> Our network guy setup a VPN server. He setup the SSH connection icon for
> every servers on the VPN web page. When click at "SSH to server" icon, VPN
> will connect through SSH to that server. The problem is, none of Linux
> servers can connect to SSH through VPN server. Other Unix servers (HP-UX,
> Solaris, AIX...) are connecting fine SSH through VPN. When connecting SSH to
> Linux (Suse, RedHat) servers from VPN, get this error "connecting to
> connection closed".
> 
> Another problem, "pointing finger!" I told him, the problem is his VPN
> setup. He told me, it is my Linux servers...blah, blah, blah...
> 
> My Linux servers are wide open for SSH. Is there anything there on my Linux
> servers preventing SSH access through VPN server? Do I need to do anything
> to allow SSH get through VPN server?
> 
> Thanks for your help.

I use ssh over Openvpn (which uses ssl), and beyond a lot of
complications involving setting up certifications on the machine,
it works fine.  As others mentioned, try ssh -vvv for debugging. 
But before that, you should try pinging and traceroute and nmap
and other tools to make sure that the ports are open, not firewalled,
etc.  You can also telnet to port 22 and see if you get an ssh prompt.
You might also learn more about Openvpn - the documentation and 
cookbooks are fairly good, and might provide a clue about SSL-based
VPNs and Linux.

Keith

Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

Subject: [PLUG] Need Help "SSH through VPN"
In-Reply-To: <a49cba240703051509p2ee35711xa1803d23df18682f@mail.gmail.com>
References: <a49cba240703051441v183a709en95c8697202a4b610@mail.gmail.com>

Message-ID: <200703060943.58275.carla@bratgrrl.com>

On Monday 05 March 2007 15:09, Jenifer Chung wrote:
> Hi Drew,
>
> Yes, the Network Admin guy setup the VPN web page. The VPN gear is Juniper
> SA-4000 SSL-VPN.
>
> Jeni

I suspect, from wading through the voluminous but largely content-free 
documentation on their Web site, that this is not a true VPN, but an SSL 
portal, because it claims "No client-software deployments." A true VPN 
requires that both server and client authenticate to each other. The vast 
majority of commercial SSL VPNs are not VPNs at all, but prettified Web 
browsers that allow arbitrary clients to login. Call me old-fashioned and 
grumpy, but the idea of letting users log in from public terminals or any old 
PC that you have no control over is insane, and paying tens of thousands of 
dollars for the privilege- well, there are no words. (keyloggers, anyone? 
spyware? sheeesh)

So I'm guessing that you're SOL, because it's not a real VPN tunnel at all. A 
real VPN doesn't require a Web browser for access. Think of it as a virtual 
private Ethernet cable transporting and protecting your bits over hostile 
networks.

This is a very good paper on the subject:
OpenVPN and the SSL VPN Revolution, by Charlie Hosner
http://www.sans.org/reading_room/whitepapers/vpns/

In conclusion, sites that don't use OpenVPN are too dumb to be in business. 
Because even if this a real SSL-based VPN, it's stupid to spend wads of money 
when a superior free product like OpenVPN is available.

--

Carla Schroder

From tcslighter at gmail.com  Tue Mar  6 09:50:35 2007

Date: Tue, 6 Mar 2007 09:50:35 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Need Help "SSH through VPN"
In-Reply-To: <200703060943.58275.carla@bratgrrl.com>
References: <a49cba240703051441v183a709en95c8697202a4b610@mail.gmail.com>
	<e2aeccd60703051450s41d5e4e9r6abca5166911f3c5@mail.gmail.com>
	<a49cba240703051509p2ee35711xa1803d23df18682f@mail.gmail.com>
	<200703060943.58275.carla@bratgrrl.com>
Message-ID: <65244f100703060950w705f71fei361b44ffd43f8a18@mail.gmail.com>

In the case of Juniper SSL based VPN's, a virtual workspace can be created
for the users that allow them access to pre-determined applications that are
virtualized into a workspace.  The advantages here are that the user does
not need to be provided an IP address and has limited access to specific
hosts/applications.  Of course the disadvantage here is if they are granted
access to upload files, modify code, etc.  However, to address those
concerns about the possibility of distributing malware, rootkits, worms,
trojans, the likes, these can be effectively contained by not providing the
SSL user with an IP address (a host that cannot be be contacted within the
tunnel).  Split tunneling would be an entirely different story though.

I've run into this zillions of times, and it doesn't get any better with 
repetition. An SSL portal is not a VPN, and allowing untrusted remote clients 
access to your network is just plain dim.

If it turns out that the Juniper SA-4000 SSL-VPN is an actual VPN, I'll eat a 
nice hearty helping of crow. But the rant against SSL portals masquerading as 
VPNs is still valid. :)

From carla at bratgrrl.com  Tue Mar  6 21:01:12 2007
From: carla at bratgrrl.com (Carla Schroder)
Date: Tue, 6 Mar 2007 21:01:12 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Need Help "SSH through VPN"
In-Reply-To: <a49cba240703061409r757895e8k935f8257537b3890@mail.gmail.com>
References: <a49cba240703051441v183a709en95c8697202a4b610@mail.gmail.com>

	<a49cba240703061409r757895e8k935f8257537b3890@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <200703062101.12631.carla@bratgrrl.com>

Er...sorry for the continued ranting, because you have to deal with what you 
have, but that is braindead. SSH through a real VPN tunnel is very nice, 
because then you have fewer hassles with forwarding and punching holes in 
your firewall. With a real VPN, once the tunnel is established you run SSH, 
or whatever you want to do, just the same as on your LAN.

If "209.152.98.99" is your alleged VPN gateway and SSH stops dead there, that 
confirms that's the roadblock.

For anyone who wants a real genuine excellent VPN, OpenVPN is wonderful. Get 
the book "OpenVPN: Building and Integrating Virtual Private Networks". The 
docs on openvpn.org are pretty good, but the book is easier to understand and 
more thorough.

Carla

Well that was weird. I went to make this reply and discovered that
overnight my keyboard died. Couldn't type anything anywhere. Mouse
still worked, though. One by one I closed apps until all were shut
down, but still no keyboard. Then I logged out and when the login
screen came up I still couldn't type. I clicked to shutdown, and got a
screenfull of stuff that didn't look like error codes, but also not
what I usually see when I shut down. Finally the shutdown process hung
and I had to hit the power button. 

On rebooting everything seems to be back to normal. Wonder what it was
that caused that. I've never lost just the keyboard before. I've had
lockups and other nasties happen, but both the mouse and the keyboard
are dead. Losing just the keyboard is a first.

OK, back to what I was going to say. I launched AbiWord and opened
a .doc file, then went to save it. (That's when I discovered the
keyboard was dead.) I had options to save in a zillion formats, Word,
OOo, html, etc. So its import/export filters can do what you need. This
is AbiWord 2.4.5 on Edgy amd64. Searching in Synaptic on "abiword"
reveals that I have installed abiword-common, -gnome, -help, -plugins,
and -plugins-gnome. 

I like AbiWord a lot, but I need features of OOo. For one thing, in
AbiWord all pages in a document must have the same orientation. And
tables are not as fully featured (I use a lot of tables). But most
critical is that it does not have an export to PDF. Plus,
it has no equivalent to PowerPoint or Impress. I keep it around because
OOo 2.0.4 on Edgy amd64 has a lot of broken stuff and it's useful for
testing. Just like I keep KOffice installed, because it can open PDF
files.

example, HR departments), but I suspect that it doesn't have all of
the features of word.

the non-rtf features of an existing Word doc.  It's not 100%, but if
an app can't write all the features of a format, it probably can't
*read* the missing features either.

It could also just mean that they haven't implemented the output side
of things yet.

--Rogan

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Wed Mar  7 20:18:07 2007

> Hi All-
> Drunk from the success of getting vmware working under fedora core (thanks

> Drew-

Super simple.  Just choose "bridged" networking.  Later, when running
vmware-config.pl, go ahead and let the script build both a NAT and
a host-only network for you as well, just so you'll have the option to
use them later.

Carlos Konstanski


From bwatson1979 at gmail.com  Wed Mar  7 20:19:12 2007
From: bwatson1979 at gmail.com (Benjamin Watson)
Date: Wed, 7 Mar 2007 22:19:12 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] More vmware advice
In-Reply-To: <e2aeccd60703071959ue8f632fv5d7241d1441c1792@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e2aeccd60703071959ue8f632fv5d7241d1441c1792@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <334c4450703072019r5a7ad15ava143d92408c6bb29@mail.gmail.com>

I run VMWare Server 1.0.1 on a Windows XP host serving a Ubuntu Guest.

I'm on a school network, but came across your particular scenario as I
wanted the VM accessible beyond the Host machine.  You can configure
the network settings during the VM build, or after, it doesn't matter
really.

Anyhow, for what you describe, I think you'll want to specify the
bridged connection.  In my setup, both the Host and Guest have the
same IP address.  Therefore, since I don't have any web server running
on my Windows Host box, all web traffic directed toward the shared IP
address is picked up by my VM Guest running apache.

However, you can also specify that the VM get its own IP address as
well.  You'd do this from within the VM guest using the traditional
tools available in the guest OS.

HTH,

Ben

From ron at Opus1.COM  Wed Mar  7 20:19:41 2007
From: ron at Opus1.COM (Ronald Chmara)

In-Reply-To: <e2aeccd60703071959ue8f632fv5d7241d1441c1792@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e2aeccd60703071959ue8f632fv5d7241d1441c1792@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <2A4D3109-E6CC-4EF3-A970-C65DF3155C49@opus1.com>

On Mar 7, 2007, at 7:59 PM, drew wymore wrote:
> Hi All-
> Drunk from the success of getting vmware working under fedora core  
> (thanks
> to everyone who helped!) I'm attempting my next adventure. I'd like to
> install a VM (easy enough) but I confused on the networking setup.  
> I'd like
> this VM to have its own public IP so I have no idea which option(s) to
> choose during setup in order to accomplish this. The guest (linux)  
> will be
> running on a linux host w/ public IP as well so I'm not sure if  
> there any
> caveats to this setup? Google has so far failed me so any pointers  
> to docs
> would be appreciated.

Sounds like you want all traffic "Bridged" into your VM, after you  
give that VM a static/public IP. If you used "Host only", only the  
host running the VM could talk to it, and if you used NAT then you'd  
have to go through some serious contortions to make sure packets from  
the public got to your VM.

HTH,
-Ronabop

On Mon, 2007-03-05 at 16:39 -0800, Quentin Hartman wrote:
> It's possibly a routing thing. I've had to setup static routes to make
> machines aware of routes to machines via hardware VPN's before. Does the
> error message pop up right away, or is there a long timeout?

Routing differences would be my first guess.  Can you compare 'netstat
-rn' on the AIX and Linux boxes to see if there are any special routes?
Also, you might check the firewall settings on your Linux boxes; AIX
comes up wide open by default, but a lot of Linux distributors these
days enable a fairly restrictive firewall by default.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Thu Mar  8 09:47:43 2007
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Thu, 8 Mar 2007 09:47:43 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] DST Sunday morning - Check your system, Win users beware
Message-ID: <20070308174743.GA12974@gate.kl-ic.com>


As you know, they changed the algorithm for daylight savings time
and it starts this weekend, two weeks earlier than previous years. 
Folks with older distros or who have not recently upgraded may want
to check their time change dates with:

zdump -v /etc/localtime | grep 2007

On my laptop, I get:

/etc/localtime  Sun Mar 11 09:59:59 2007 UTC = Sun Mar 11 01:59:59 2007 PST isdst=0 gmtoff=-28800
/etc/localtime  Sun Mar 11 10:00:00 2007 UTC = Sun Mar 11 03:00:00 2007 PDT isdst=1 gmtoff=-25200
/etc/localtime  Sun Nov  4 08:59:59 2007 UTC = Sun Nov  4 01:59:59 2007 PDT isdst=1 gmtoff=-25200
/etc/localtime  Sun Nov  4 09:00:00 2007 UTC = Sun Nov  4 01:00:00 2007 PST isdst=0 gmtoff=-28800

If you don't get the right answer, you will need to do more research
on a cure; automated updates took care of this for me.


Those of you running older Microsoft products are semi-f****d.  If
you are running Windows 2000, Exchange 2000, or Exchange 5.5, for
example, these are no longer officially supported and a patch will
cost you $4000 , according to:

http://macdailynews.com/index.php/weblog/comments/12891/

It seems that Microsoft embeds the conversion times into the 
application programs, not a global file that all applications use. 
So even "supported" systems will need a lot of program patching.

The "drive off customers to Linux/Mac" team at Redmond is apparently
working late these days.  Expect a LOT of angry Microsoft users
driving home from work Monday.  Some are calling this "mini-Y2K".

Keith

From krisa at subtend.net  Thu Mar  8 12:05:50 2007
From: krisa at subtend.net (Kris)
Date: Thu, 08 Mar 2007 12:05:50 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] DST Sunday morning - Check your system, Win users beware
In-Reply-To: <20070308174743.GA12974@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <20070308174743.GA12974@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <45F06C9E.7030602@subtend.net>

Keith Lofstrom wrote:
> As you know, they changed the algorithm for daylight savings time
> and it starts this weekend, two weeks earlier than previous years. 
> Folks with older distros or who have not recently upgraded may want
> to check their time change dates with:

If anyone is brave enough to be running GroupWise under Linux, you will
need:

"DST Changes are in GW 7.0.1 IR1 GWIA & Webaccess release patch date of
21 December 2006 or newer."

You get the whole SDD of Groupwise with that download.  Seems that it
installs new binaries (rpm's) and doesn't touch the domain or PO areas
(no wpX.db files are changed).  If you already have 7.0.1, no display
tells you that it is now 7.0.1ir1, so you can verify by looking at the
date on the RPM's installed, `rpm -qa|grep novell`.  eDirectory and
Groupwise clients use the system time (SuSE/Windows updates).

Gaining this knowledge was not a choice. :)  Viva la FOSS!

-- 
I'm just a packet pusher.

On Thu, 2007-03-08 at 09:47 -0800, Keith Lofstrom wrote:

> If you don't get the right answer, you will need to do more research
> on a cure; automated updates took care of this for me.

The timezone files seem to be a reasonably stable binary format (at
least, within the same bit-width), so you can update older systems by
copying the appropriate timezone file (/usr/share/zoneinfo/US/Pacific)
to the older hosts.  I had to do this with an old Caldera OpenLinux
(pre-mad-SCO disease) box and SuSE 9.1 box.

Wil

From rsteff at comcast.net  Thu Mar  8 17:16:26 2007
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Thu, 08 Mar 2007 17:16:26 -0800
Subject: Resolved: [PLUG] Open Office Modifications
In-Reply-To: <45EC3A90.2070002@comcast.net>
References: <45EC3A90.2070002@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <45F0B56A.90208@comcast.net>

Richard C. Steffens wrote:
> Is there a way to change the behavior of the <ENTER> key in OOcalc?
> 
> In Excel, if one tabs from column to column while entering data and then
>  hits <ENTER>, the active cell becomes the cell below the one from which
> tabbing began. In OOcalc, <ENTER> just moves you to the cell below the
> one you were on when you hit <ENTER>.

I posted this question to users at openoffice.org and got a few responses.
One of them came close enough that, with modifications, it solves my
problem. One of the users replied:

> I was able to obtain a similar behavior by placing
> the "Crtl+Left Arrow"
> followed by a "Down Arrow" keyboard shortcuts in a macro and assigning
> it to a new keyboard shortcut "Shift+Enter"

If I reverse the order, i.e. start with <Down Arrow> and follow with
<Ctrl+Left Arrow> I get close to what I want. <Ctrl+Left Arrow> stops
when it encounters data. For my application this will work most of the
time, since there is almost always some data in the cell to the left of
the one I want to go to and rarely any data to the right of that cell.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens

On booting (Grub line has "quiet no splash") I suddenly got a couple
screenfuls of the following:

udevd[2216] add-to-rules: unknown 'attrs{idProduct}'

The same line repeated for about a screenful worth on shutdown, but
after restarting, shutting down, and restarting a few times, it now
happens only on bootup. In spite of what appears to be an error
message, the computer seems to operate fine.

Whatever it means, it was caused by something in the following: Edgy
amd64 announced that I had half a dozen upgrades. I was applying the
upgrades with Synaptic when the computer locked up -- dead keyboard and
mouse, no disk activity. I had to hit the power button.

When Grub came back up I decided to run memtest. I have never done this
before, but I recently ran into a webpage suggesting that memory might
be a cause of lockups -- and I have one original 256 MB stick and one 1
GB replacement stick. Maybe there is a memory mismatch or something. So
I ran memtest one pass, a little over an hour. No errors, so I went
ahead and booted. That is when the above message suddenly appeared.

Google tells me that udevd is some kind of utility, but I don't
understand what it does. And the rest of it is in Greek. But if I
understood it I bet I would know what is wrong and have a fair chance
of fixing it.

Jason,

  I looked at the man pages for udev, udevd, udevinfo, and udevmonitor. 
Basically, udev is the program that handles devices dynamically. This is 
how we are able to plug in digital cameras, thumb drives, ipods, etc. 
and have them magically be mounted and available. You might find 
something useful in the output of "udevinfo -e".

Jason-
As Mel mentioned udev is used to dynamically create devices in the /proc
filesystem. AFAIK its only for 2.6 kernels but I may be wrong. I found
exactly 1 hit on google after change a few parameters for the search based
on your error message and its a post to an ubuntu forum about a similar but
not exact udev problem

https://answers.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+ticket/3801

May be worthwhile checking into. Maybe udev was part of the upgrade packages
you installed and there's a bug perhaps? It seems like to me from the text
you posted that udev is unable to create a device node for something
installed on the computer because it can't determine its device attributes
but I could be completely wrong.

Drew-

udev rules and the seemingly arbitrary changes introduced in their
syntax and structure have frustrated many people for quite some time.
Personally, I've not yet found it necessary to mess with them, happily,
so I remain blissfully ignorant until it someday bites me on the ass.
There's some good, thorough documentation here:

http://www.reactivated.net/writing_udev_rules.html

I'm not sure what "[2216]" means, but the "attr{idProduct}" would seem
to indicate, as Drew suggested, that udev is missing an attribute for
some device you have, or it thinks it is.  Basically, you use udevinfo
to determine the various attributes of any particular device you want to
write a rule for.  Then you use those attributes to contruct a rule.
So, for example:

~$ udevinfo -a -p /sys/block/sda

Udevinfo starts with the device specified by the devpath and then
walks up the chain of parent devices. It prints for every device
found, all possible attributes in the udev rules key format.
A rule to match, can be composed by the attributes of the device
and the attributes from one single parent device.

  looking at device '/block/sda':
    KERNEL=="sda"
    SUBSYSTEM=="block"
    DRIVER==""
    ATTR{stat}==" 2170526   295139 130531751 14838764  3096316 14664226
142239082 87592236        0 11373572 102465456"
    ATTR{size}=="312581808"
    ATTR{removable}=="0"
    ATTR{range}=="16"
    ATTR{dev}=="8:0"

  looking at parent device
'/devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0f.0/host0/target0:0:0/0:0:0:0':
    KERNELS=="0:0:0:0"
    SUBSYSTEMS=="scsi"
    DRIVERS=="sd"
    ATTRS{ioerr_cnt}=="0x0"
    ATTRS{iodone_cnt}=="0x505da8"
    ATTRS{iorequest_cnt}=="0x505da8"
    ATTRS{iocounterbits}=="32"
    ATTRS{timeout}=="30"
    ATTRS{state}=="running"
    ATTRS{rev}=="08.0"
    ATTRS{model}=="WDC WD1600JD-22H"
    ATTRS{vendor}=="ATA     "
    ATTRS{scsi_level}=="6"
    ATTRS{type}=="0"
    ATTRS{queue_type}=="none"
    ATTRS{queue_depth}=="1"
    ATTRS{device_blocked}=="0"
[more results snipped]

That gives you a whole bunch of attributes you can use to construct your
rules.  "Product" is one of those attributes, but your udevd specifies
"idProduct".  Maybe it's just the name of the attribute that has
changed.

My bet would be that something in Ubuntu's new init system, Upstart[1],
has not quite meshed with udev.  Probably just a little bug they need to
fix, or a messed-up script somewhere.  But that's the price of living on
the bleeding edge.

[1]  What a lousy name!  It brings back memories of Microsoft using the
Stone's "Start Me Up" in their Windows 95 campaign.

For Synaptic I would look around /var/log as thats where most log files are
generally kept. I would almost be certain that there's some sort of
transaction log. I know Slackware and Fedora Core have both implemented this
so that there are time stamped logs of when a particular package was
installed.  You may want to scope out /etc/udev/rules.d which is where those
rules live on my boxen and see if the time stamp is from today or gives any
clue as to when it might have last been changed.

I'm almost certain that 2216 is referring to the process ID however if its
the same on every boot then of course that wouldn't be the case.

Drew-

 John-
libgphoto2-port0 is used by libgphoto to access usb and serial devices so i
think based on what you found in the rules directory that the error is
either a serial port or usb issue. Do you have any USB devices plugged into
your laptop? If so I'd start by unplugging them one by one and see if the
error goes away.

>>
>> The timezone files seem to be a reasonably stable binary format (at
>> least, within the same bit-width), so you can update older systems by
>> copying the appropriate timezone file (/usr/share/zoneinfo/US/Pacific)
>> to the older hosts.  I had to do this with an old Caldera OpenLinux
>> (pre-mad-SCO disease) box and SuSE 9.1 box.
>
> There is always the method of changing the value of the TZ environment
> variable. Not as nice as automatic changing, but effective in the worst
> case.

That works for Unix machines.  It does not work as well for Windows 
machines.

Here is a post from Perl-5-Porters about it...

From: 	Jan Dubois <jand at activestate.com>
To: 	perl5-porters at perl.org
Subject: 	What I learned about Windows and Daylight Saving Time 
today...
Date: 	Mon, 5 Mar 2007 14:47:49 -0800


Prompted by a bug report regarding the new DST rules I had a closer
look how localtime() determines DST on Windows.  Below is my analysis
of the sorry state of affairs, as far as I can tell.

I guess for the vast majority of Windows users this just means that
DST will be wrong for older timestamps.  I'm not sure how important
that is though.  Providing a proper workaround probably means that
we would have to use the DateTime::TimeZone module within localtime().

=====================================================================
The daylight saving time (DST) for the localtime() function is
determined by the C runtime library function of the same name.

This function has 2 different operating modes:

1) The TZ environment variable has been set.

In this case MSVCRT calculates DST itself, based on the USA rules.
The latest released version (as of (March 5th 2007) of MSVCRT.dll has
not yet been updated for the 2007 DST rules.  The localtime() function
will still apply the old rules to 2007.  Microsoft claims to have a
hotfix for this, that is available from Microsoft Customer Support
Services only:

    http://support.microsoft.com/kb/932590

2) The TZ environment variable has *not* been set.

In this case MSVCRT retrieves the DST transition times from the
GetTimeZoneInformation() API:

     http://msdn2.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ms724421.aspx

This API only provides the transition times according to the *current*
DST rules.  There is no database of historical transition times.  That
means that localtime() applied to previous years will use the new
transition times even for old timestamps.

Windows Vista (and Longhorn Server) support a new API called
GetDynamicTimeZoneInformation() that implements a database of historic
DST rules.  It is not known if the hotfix mentioned above will make
use of this API when running on Vista.
=====================================================================

Cheers,
-Jan

-- 
"Invoking the supernatural can explain anything, and hence explains nothing."
                   - University of Utah bioengineering professor Gregory Clark

From rsteff at comcast.net  Fri Mar  9 16:07:48 2007
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Fri, 09 Mar 2007 16:07:48 -0800
Subject: Resolved: [PLUG] CUPS Password Problem

> Carla Schroder wrote:
>> On Friday 09 March 2007 11:16, Richard C. Steffens wrote:
>>> What does one do when CUPS doesn't recognize root's password?
> <...>
>> I wonder if SUSE did the same dim thing as Ubuntu Dapper and older, which 
>> (stupidly) disabled the root password in CUPS and the CUPS web interface. 

Sure enough, SuSE did change how CUPS runs.

>From the SuSE documentation found on my machine:

----------------------------------------------------------------------------
11.6.2.1. cupsd Runs as the User lp

 On start-up, cupsd changes from the user root to the user lp. This
provides a much higher level of security, because the CUPS print service
does not run with unrestricted permissions, only with the permissions
needed for the print service.

However, the authentication (the password check) cannot be performed via
/etc/shadow, because lp has no access to /etc/shadow. Instead, the
CUPS-specific authentication via /etc/cups/passwd.md5 must be used. For
this purpose, a CUPS administrator with the CUPS administration group
sys and a CUPS password must be entered in /etc/cups/passwd.md5. To do
this, enter the following as root:
lppasswd -g sys -a CUPS-admin-name

 This setting is also essential if you want to use the CUPS
administration Web front-end or the KDE printer administration tool.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Once I created the user and password I was able to log in to "Do
Administration Tasks" at http://localhost:631/ and add the printer. The
test page printed just fine.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens

started. Then, after I realized I didn't want it to be known as dhccp4
(or something like that -- what was assigned by my router), I couldn't
find a way to change it in the XP driver. There's a way to change it
from the printer's front panel, which is simple enough, but no way I
could find to change where the computer was told to look for it. In the
troubleshooting section of the web site, the recommendation was to
uninstall the driver and reinstall it! That worked. On the other hand,
the Win98 driver install went very smoothly. Of course, by this time I
had already changed the printer's IP address, and knew to pay attention
to that during the driver install.

Or their security engineers.  Not running processes as root that do not
need to be is a good thing.  The inability to read /etc/shadow and
authenticate with it is a minor inconvenience; there are other ways they
could have made it work more transparently.  OTOH, not allowing root to
login remotely with the usual root password on a service that doesn't
log authentication via syslog is also probably good.

From: Palm Inc <PalmInc at news.palmnewsletters.com>
Date: Mar 10, 2007 3:29 AM
Subject: Daylight Saving Time--Palm Device Update Required


Palm(R)

**********************************************************************
NEW Daylight Saving Time changes - Palm(R) device update required!
**********************************************************************

You are receiving this product-related message because our records
indicate that you have purchased and/or registered a Palm device.

Daylight Saving Time (DST) begins March 11, 2007 -- three weeks
earlier than last year. DST will also last one week longer in the
fall as well, changing back to standard time on November 11, 2007.

To help your calendar events and email reflect these new DST changes,
please visit the link below to download the DST update for all Palm(R)
devices. Remember, your device will NOT update automatically, so
please download this update from Palm.com before March 11:
http://News.palmnewsletters.com/cgi-bin13/DM/y/ekJl0WBzvf0HXH0Zlu0Gi

From linux at frankhunt.com  Sat Mar 10 12:37:26 2007
From: linux at frankhunt.com (Frank Hunt)
Date: Sat, 10 Mar 2007 15:37:26 -0500
Subject: [PLUG] DST Sunday morning - Check your system, Win users beware
In-Reply-To: <45F306B9.5090000@comcast.net>
References: <200703090248.l292mh2K060993@m5p.com>	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0703090857480.22114@blackbox.fnordora.org>
	<45F306B9.5090000@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <45F31706.2010906@frankhunt.com>


NTP operates on UTC, not local time.  NTP packets to not contain 
information regarding local time zone offset or DST rollover 
information.  It is up to the local system to provide the local time - 
by way of offset from UTC.  For Pacific, that's 8 for standard time and 
7 for daylight savings time.  It is up to the local system to adjust the 
offset from 8 to 7 in the spring and 7 to 8 in the fall.  That's the 
rub.  Then, of course, there's JRE which does it's own time thing.


Richard C. Steffens wrote:
> If my computers are checking in with a time standard on the Internet,
> won't that solve the problem?
> 

-- 
frank hunt
PLUG member-in-absentia
confused linux admin
part time windows(r) washer
rochester hills, mi

You can download tzedit.exe from out on the internets and run it on your 
win98 box(s) - it edits the table that contains the offsets and the 
dates when they are engaged.  Then there's all the other stuff you might 
have with time in it - I just noticed that appointments in my handy HP 
iPAQ are all off by one hour starting Monday.  But then it runs Windoze 
so . . .

Misunderstanding why people bypass the RFC's can become a major
contributor to the spam problem.  If we aren't on the same page,
what you do and what I do to address spam will be incompatible and
when these efforts fail, they discourage both of us from trying
to filter out spam at all.  I run my own mail server and the
recommendation I have run into is to use the whois.rfc-ignorant
blacklist.

You are saying that making the source of email more identifiable
increases spam, am I correct?

From plug_0 at robinson-west.com  Fri Mar  9 18:36:53 2007
From: plug_0 at robinson-west.com (plug_0 at robinson-west.com)
Date: Fri, 09 Mar 2007 18:36:53 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Bind behavior...
Message-ID: <20070309183653.m0baehw8gssw4oo8@web.robinson-west.com>

My impression, someone please step in and correct me if I am wrong, is that
bind 9.3 is supposed to hand out your mail exchanger records in order and
not shuffle them.

My brother and I are attempting to be backup mail exchanger sites for each
other and waddya know, we are finding that mail to site A ends up trying to
go through site B even when A is still up.

So we have...

foo.com. MX 30 mail.bar.com
foo.com. MX 20 mail2.foo.com
foo.com. MX 10 mail1.foo.com

at one site ( The domains aren't really foo and bar. )

And

bar.com. MX 30 mail2.foo.com
bar.com. MX 20 mail1.foo.com
bar.com. MX 10 mail1.bar.com

at the other site.

Now, our theory going in for someone trying to email a person on say foo
is that their ISP's mail server won't go to bar unless foo is down.
Apparently, our bind servers hand out the mail exchangers in shuffled
order.  I guess the weights are included with this list, but they seem
to be getting ignored wholesale.  Is there some way to disable shuffling
in bind 9?  Is it possible to get the average smtp server out on the
Internet to use the mail exhangers for a particular domain in order?

Can a specific order be enforced when it comes to which mail excahnger for
a particular domain gets tried first, second,...?

----------------------------------------------------------------
This message was sent using IMP, the Internet Messaging Program.

>From: alan <alan at clueserver.org>

> > There is always the method of changing the value of the TZ environment
> > variable. Not as nice as automatic changing, but effective in the worst
> > case.
> 
> That works for Unix machines.  It does not work as well for Windows

There of course is the true fix that is permanent and patches pretty well
everything. Getting rid of DST. Fixing it for the whole country would be
best, but failing that doing it at the state level works too.

Alas I've been dragged out of Oregon, but I've still got the details
handy. You need to write to your legislator and ask them to amend
ORS 187.110, to exempt Oregon from 15 U.S.C. 260a (the national law
explicitly allows states to exempt themselves). Seems I need the
equivalent section of California law now.  :-/

> something, you could try moving the libgphoto rules out of /etc/udev/rules.d

I was going to take your suggestion, but decided to wait until after I
finished a big project that I needed the computer for. This evening I
finished it and, just for kicks and giggles, launched the Update
Manager. Guess what? New versions of libgphoto*. I'm pretty sure those
were in the upgrades I did just before this mess started. 

I installed the new ones, then shut down and restarted. No more error
messages. I could go sniff around in Ubuntu bug trackers to be sure,
but it looks like someone at Ubuntu put new libgphoto files in the
reppositories before they were ready for prime time, and the ones I
just upgraded to are a hasty fix.

Thanks for all the advice and suggestions. At least I learned something
more about Linux. Like "don't be in such a hurry to install an
upgrade." :)

and got:

/etc/localtime  Sun Mar 11 09:59:59 2007 UTC = Sun Mar 11 01:59:59 2007 PST 
isdst=0 gmtoff=-28800
/etc/localtime  Sun Mar 11 10:00:00 2007 UTC = Sun Mar 11 03:00:00 2007 PDT 
isdst=1 gmtoff=-25200
/etc/localtime  Sun Nov  4 08:59:59 2007 UTC = Sun Nov  4 01:59:59 2007 PDT 
isdst=1 gmtoff=-25200
/etc/localtime  Sun Nov  4 09:00:00 2007 UTC = Sun Nov  4 01:00:00 2007 PST 
isdst=0 gmtoff=-28800

Which I presume is the right answer.

Why does my machine still display a time which looks like standard time?

Run "date" in a shell.  Does that give the right answer?

From griffint at pobox.com  Sun Mar 11 10:55:57 2007
From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Sun, 11 Mar 2007 10:55:57 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] DST
In-Reply-To: <45F41FE8.7040706@dslnorthwest.net>
References: <45F418A5.2050804@dslnorthwest.net> <86abyj22nh.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
	<45F41FE8.7040706@dslnorthwest.net>
Message-ID: <200703111055.58111.griffint@pobox.com>

On Sunday 11 March 2007 8:27:36 am Denis Heidtmann wrote:
> [snip]
> > Run "date" in a shell.  Does that give the right answer?
>
> I get:
> Sun Mar 11 08:22:42 PDT 2007
> Strange.  My watch says 8:22, but I did not reset it this AM.  And my VCR,
> which gets time from the transmitted signal shows 8:22 as well. It looks
> like the only thing that has changed is PST -> PDT, an S becomes a D.
>

If your computer was powered off at 2:00 AM *and* your hardware clock
is set to local time instead of UTC, then it would have missed the change.
The computer now thinks it is on PDT, but on boot-up it synced to the
hardware clock which was still on PST.

That's why it's usually better to have the hardware clock set to UTC. Unless 
you are dual booting to Windows, then the advantage/disadvantage balance
tilts toward having the hardware clock set to local time.

Terry

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Sun Mar 11 21:11:52 2007
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Sun, 11 Mar 2007 21:11:52 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Working around borked nameservers, clearing caches
In-Reply-To: <20070309200006.467DE4345@ulke.nakedape.cc>
References: <20070309200006.467DE4345@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <20070312041152.GA2337@gate.kl-ic.com>


This weekend I was at a motel in Bend, which had free wifi.  The
problem was, the nameserver was broken - it returned incorrect
IP addresses for most names (en.wikipedia.org = 1.0.0.0, for 
example) .  I could still connect to numeric IP addresses, though.

I could still drive a VPN to my server, so I copied the
appropriate IP addresses from /etc/resolv.conf over to my
laptop on the VPN link.  That meant that new names resolved
correctly, but the old addresses still pointed at the
borked IP addresses given by the balky nameserver; the bad
translations were apparently cached somewhere.

My experience with nameservers is with named and such;  I
recently changed over to 2.6.9/RHEL4.4 and don't know where
the name service cache sits, or how to flush it (it seems
to survive through a reboot).  So the question:

??? How do you flush the namserver cache on 2.6.9/RHEL4.4 ? 

Keith

PS:  am no longer at the motel, so this is mostly of academic
interest, but I might encounter a bad nameserver in the future
to clean up after.

> is still on standard time. Everything else seems to be on daylight

I have to maintain some long-dead distro versions (RH 7.2, RH 8, FC 3) 
in order to keep some proprietary software running.

I just downloaded the raw updated zoneinfo files, ran them through 
zic, and installed them over the rpm-installed files. crond needs to 
be restarted to see the new files -- the same for syslogd and most 
other daemons.

Yeah, manual file installation breaks rpm control, but these machines 
are all on life support anyway...

That is an accurate answer, but I think I mistakenly asked the
wrong question.  I don't have rndc or named on my laptop.  Those
were on RH9 2.4.22, but not on RHEL4.4 2.6.9.  I have the nscd
(name service cache daemon) program on my laptop, but "nscd -g"
says nscd is not running. 

I am not sure, but I think I am trying to find the "DNS resolver"
cache for my 2.6.9 kernel, see:
    http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNS#Broken_resolvers

Since both ping and firefox were giving me the bad IP addresses,
it is probably something the kernel hooks up to, though since it
persists through reboots it is probably a cache outside of the
kernel itself.  "man resolver" (and gethostbyname),  doesn't tell
me about cache files.  I've looked at much other stuff, and may
have to dive into kernel source to answer the question.  Yikes!

I have SELINUX enabled, if that makes any difference, I don't 
understand SELINUX (we need a PLUG presentation).  Perhaps that
doesn't work with a hand-edited /etc/resolv.conf file unless I
take extra steps.  When I look at sbin/dhclient-script, for
example, I see "/sbin/restorecon /etc/resolv.conf" after that
script modifies /etc/resolv.conf .   Is this important?

So, the modified question:

??? How do you flush the dns resolver cache on 2.6.9/RHEL4.4
??? with SELINUX enabled?

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Mon Mar 12 09:41:20 2007
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Mon, 12 Mar 2007 09:41:20 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Working around borked nameservers, clearing caches
In-Reply-To: <20070312155943.GA10119@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <20070309200006.467DE4345@ulke.nakedape.cc>
	<20070312041152.GA2337@gate.kl-ic.com>
	<e2aeccd60703120152j661dae8cm1d10aef4082cc572@mail.gmail.com>
	<20070312155943.GA10119@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0703120935010.20379@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Mon, 12 Mar 2007, Keith Lofstrom wrote:

> That is an accurate answer, but I think I mistakenly asked the wrong
> question.  I don't have rndc or named on my laptop.  Those were on RH9
> 2.4.22, but not on RHEL4.4 2.6.9.  I have the nscd (name service cache
> daemon) program on my laptop, but "nscd -g" says nscd is not running.

> ??? How do you flush the dns resolver cache on 2.6.9/RHEL4.4 with SELINUX
> ??? enabled?

Keith,

   I don't have the answer to that question, but perhaps what I've done would
be of interest to you.

   On my notebook, I copy /etc/resolv.conf to /etc/resolve.conf.office. This
is the list of dns servers I use in the office on all hosts.

   When I travel, I always need to run (as root) 'dhcpcd -d ethx' (where x ==
0 || x == 1 depending on whether the connection is wired or wireless) to get
an IP address for my location. Frequently, this overwrites /etc/resolve.conf
with the hotel's/airport's/coffee shop's DNS server names. I let them
happily overwrite each other. When I return to the office, I copy
resolv.conf.office to resolv.conf and I'm back to where I need to be.

   It ain't sophisticaled, but it's been working for me for several years
now.

Rich

Message-ID: <48180.10.8.0.2.1173721488.squirrel@chinook>

Even though my FC3 system had all the correct updates, I had to
re-run the time-zone selection utility to re-select America/Los Angeles
in order to get it to stick system-wide.

Some of my processes had TZ=PST8PDT which is why they worked. But
processes without a TZ setting used the system default time zone,
which was a cached copy of the old time zone settings for
America/Los Angeles. Rerunning the time-zone selection utility
updated the cached copy. The package update ought to have taken
care of this, but since fedora-legacy is now dead there's not
anyone to complain to.

Terry

On Sat, Mar 10, 2007 at 07:41:13PM -0800, Elliott Mitchell wrote:

> There of course is the true fix that is permanent and patches pretty well
> everything. Getting rid of DST. Fixing it for the whole country would be
> best, but failing that doing it at the state level works too.

As I understand it, that process requires a:

 cd /state/representatives/
 tar -xvf newrepresentatives.tar

This is, I am told, because consumers shop more during daylight
hours, and it is better business to send them to work in darkness
and have them come home past the stores in the waning daylight.
Employers want their people awake, so start times at businesses
compensate over time by starting the day later.  The direction of
movement indicates the relative strength of production businesses
versus retail businesses and their respective lobbying power.

100 years from now, we will have daylight savings savings savings
savings time, the sun will come up at 2PM, and we will go to work
at 3PM, and go home at 12PM, past the stores in waning daylight.  
Going to work at 3PM is standard programmers hours now, so for
these workers there will be no change.  :-)

Keith

>>>>> "Keith" == Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com> writes:

Keith> 100 years from now, we will have daylight savings savings
Keith> savings savings time, the sun will come up at 2PM, and we will
Keith> go to work at 3PM, and go home at 12PM, [...]

Quibble: 12PM (admitting some ambiguity) should properly be regarded
as Noon, rather than midnight.  While the stroke of noon could
reasonably be regarded as neither ante nor post meridian, all those
12:foo:bar.baz times _are_ post meridian and therefore it makes sense
on my personal planet to regard the instant of meridian as lumped in
with its neighbors.

But then again, real sanity in our temporal labelling schemes will
only arrive with the adoption of the French Revolutionary Calendar as
well as the metric clock.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Mon Mar 12 16:04:14 2007
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Mon, 12 Mar 2007 16:04:14 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] DNS resolver cache, and poisoned nameservers
Message-ID: <20070312230414.GC14024@gate.kl-ic.com>


PLUGgers:

I forwarded a similar question about borked DNS resolution to
the Scientific Linux mailing group, and got a great response,
forwarded below.  My solution might not be available to most
people.  However, there might be DNS servers out there on
alternate ports to UDP 53, and a expedient IP tables fix might
work for others, too.

Keith

----- Forwarded message from Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com> -----

> On 3/12/07, Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com> wrote:
> >This weekend at a motel with free wifi, the nameserver was broken
> >and spewing some incorrect IP addresses ( wikipedia = 1.0.0.0
> >for example ).  Traffic to numeric IP addresses flowed normally.
> >
> >I attempted a workaround by putting known-good nameservers in
> >/etc/resolv.conf .  Unfortunately, I still saw a lot of borked
> >DNS resolution, and surfing and pinging sites that I had attempted
> >before the fix resulted in the same errors.  The errors persisted
> >over a reboot.
 
On Mon, Mar 12, 2007 at 04:18:28PM -0600, Stephen John Smoogen wrote:
> A lot of hotels use DNS proxies and/or network trafficing to make sure
> all/most DNS goes to their ISP's DNS server. I found this at the last
> couple of Motels I have been at.. where putting in any DNS servers or
> using the Caching-nameserver to use the root servers directly..
> didn't. At some hotels, all traffic was lost.. at some I would see it
> in the case of 4 out of 10 or so calls would get routed silently to
> their servers.
> 
> >I recently converted from RH9 2.4.22 to SL4.4 2.6.9 , and I don't
> >know how the new system does DNS resolution (it appears to be in
> >the kernel instead of a separate program like named) and how SELINUX
> 
> Linux usually uses the following system:
> 
> Program calls glibc which calls some subset of named instructions.
> These then use the ips listed in /etc/resolv.conf to grab DNS anmes.
> 
> However in most hotels cases, this doesnt work because while your
> packet thinks its going to say 129.24.8.1.. all UDP for port 53 goes
> to 10.0.0.1 and gets rewritten back to you so it looks like it came
> from 129.24.8.1

So there wasn't really a cache on my machine at all.  Interesting.

This suggests a fix.  I usually set up a VPN back to my server when
I am remote (and it worked this time, too, because I use numeric IP
addresses to get there).  If I use iptables rules to forward all UDP
port 53 traffic to my own server, through the VPN, I can bypass a
balky DNS server.  A little slower, but more reliable.

Thanks for the very helpful response!

Keith

dmesg shows device names for USB storage devices (your scanner is not
one of these, I know).  I have here a snippet of dmesg output for my
6-slot card reader, for example:

scsi 2:0:0:0: Direct-Access     Y-E DATA CF Card Reader   1.03 PQ: 0 ANSI: 2
sd 2:0:0:0: Attached scsi removable disk sda
sd 2:0:0:0: Attached scsi generic sg0 type 0
scsi 2:0:0:1: Direct-Access     Y-E DATA SM Card Reader   1.03 PQ: 0 ANSI: 2
sd 2:0:0:1: Attached scsi removable disk sdb
sd 2:0:0:1: Attached scsi generic sg1 type 0
scsi 2:0:0:2: Direct-Access     Y-E DATA MS Card Reader   1.03 PQ: 0 ANSI: 2
sd 2:0:0:2: Attached scsi removable disk sdc
sd 2:0:0:2: Attached scsi generic sg2 type 0
scsi 2:0:0:3: Direct-Access     Y-E DATA SD Card Reader   1.03 PQ: 0 ANSI: 2
sd 2:0:0:3: Attached scsi removable disk sdd
sd 2:0:0:3: Attached scsi generic sg3 type 0
usb-storage: device scan complete

And if I go to /usr/src/linux/drivers/usb/ and issue:

     grep -nr -e 'device scan complete' *

I find this:

     storage/usb.c:936: printk(KERN_DEBUG "usb-storage: device scan complete\n");

If you can find any debug info at all re: your scanner in dmesg or
/var/log/messages, perhaps a snippet of generic text will lead you
right to the kernel code that outputs it.  Who knows what tantalyzing
leads may develop from this.

> > From: Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com>
> >  My scanner is now plugged into a USB port on the rear of the motherboard,
> > along with a web cam. Because of permissions problems, I -- a mere user --
> > cannot use them. I will change permissions to allow me access to these

Check out this thread: http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=91948

Once you can identify your device, you can use udev as described in
that thread (And the book Ubuntu Hacks) to both mount it where you
want it, and also give it the permissions you want, using the MODE
attribute.

Perhaps this is overkill for the problem you're having, but I think it
is the most elegant solution, at least for systems using udev.

Regards -- Andy
